```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# big-code-kafka-refac-001: Rename RecordAccumulator to BatchAccumulator in Apache Kafka

## Task

Rename the `RecordAccumulator` class to `BatchAccumulator` throughout the Apache Kafka producer subsystem. The `RecordAccumulator` in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` manages per-partition queues of `ProducerBatch` objects, not individual records. Its core data structure is a `ConcurrentMap<TopicPartition, Deque<ProducerBatch>>`, and its key methods (`ready()`, `drain()`, `append()`) all operate at batch granularity. Renaming to `BatchAccumulator` better describes the class's true responsibility.

The refactoring includes:
1. Rename the class `RecordAccumulator` to `BatchAccumulator` (including the file itself)
2. Rename the inner classes: `RecordAccumulator.RecordAppendResult` → `BatchAccumulator.RecordAppendResult`, `RecordAccumulator.ReadyCheckResult` → `BatchAccumulator.ReadyCheckResult`
3. Update `KafkaProducer.java` — field type, constructor, and all usages
4. Update `Sender.java` — field type, constructor parameter, and all usages
5. Update `BuiltInPartitioner.java` — RecordAccumulator references
6. Update all test files: `RecordAccumulatorTest`, `SenderTest`, `TransactionManagerTest`, `KafkaProducerTest`
7. Update the JMH benchmark: `RecordAccumulatorFlushBenchmark`
8. Update comment references in `Node.java` and `WorkerSourceTask.java`

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kafka--0753c489 (mirror of apache/kafka) (Java, ~1.2M LOC)
- **Category**: Cross-File Refactoring
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ — the Kafka producer internals

## Requirements

1. Identify ALL files that need modification for this refactoring
2. Document the complete dependency chain showing why each file is affected
3. Implement the changes (or describe them precisely if the scope is too large)
4. Verify that no references to the old API/name remain

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```

- path/to/file2.ext — why this file needs changes
...

1. Definition: path/to/definition.ext (original definition)
2. Direct usage: path/to/user1.ext (imports/references the symbol)
3. Transitive: path/to/user2.ext (uses a type that depends on the symbol)
...

## Code Changes
### path/to/file1.ext
```diff
- old code
+ new code
```

### path/to/file2.ext
```diff
- old code
+ new code
```

## Analysis
[Explanation of the refactoring strategy, affected areas, and verification approach]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File coverage: Did you identify ALL files that need modification?
- Completeness: Were all references updated (no stale references)?
- Compilation: Does the code still compile after changes?
- Correctness: Do the changes preserve the intended behavior?

     1→# Kafka Producer Refactoring: RecordAccumulator → BatchAccumulator
     2→
     3→## Executive Summary
     4→
     5→This refactoring renames the `RecordAccumulator` class to `BatchAccumulator` throughout the Apache Kafka producer subsystem. The new name better reflects the class's true responsibility: managing per-partition queues of `ProducerBatch` objects at batch granularity, not individual records.
     6→
     7→## Files Examined
     8→
     9→### Production Code
    10→- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BatchAccumulator.java** — Core class definition; renamed from RecordAccumulator.java; manages producer batches
    11→- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java** — Uses BatchAccumulator as a field; creates instances; uses BatchAccumulator.PartitionerConfig, BatchAccumulator.AppendCallbacks, BatchAccumulator.RecordAppendResult
    12→- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java** — Uses BatchAccumulator as a field; calls methods on accumulator; uses BatchAccumulator.ReadyCheckResult
    13→- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BuiltInPartitioner.java** — Comment references to BatchAccumulator partitioning logic
    14→- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java** — Comment references to BatchAccumulator batch abort logic
    15→- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/Node.java** — Comment references to BatchAccumulator.ready() performance-critical code
    16→
    17→### Test Code
    18→- **clients/src/test/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BatchAccumulatorTest.java** — Test class; renamed from RecordAccumulatorTest.java; tests BatchAccumulator fun

a new batch is created\\n261:      * <p>\\n262:      *\\n263:      * @param topic The topic to which this record is being sent\\n264:      * @param partition The partition to which this record is being sent or RecordMetadata.UNKNOWN_PARTITION\\n265:      *                  if any partition could be used\\n266:      * @param timestamp The timestamp of the record\\n267:      * @param key The key for the record\\n268:      * @param value The value for the record\\n269:      * @param headers the Headers for the record\\n270:      * @param callbacks The callbacks to execute\\n271:      * @param metadata\\n274:      */\\n275:     public RecordAppendResult append(String topic,\\n276:                                      int partition,\\n277:                                      long timestamp,\\n278:                                      byte[] key,\\n279:                                      byte[] value,\\n280:                                      Header[] headers,\\n281:                                      AppendCallbacks callbacks,\\n282:                                      long maxTimeToBlock,\\n283:                                      long nowMs,\\n284:                                      Cluster cluster) throws InterruptedException {\\n285:         TopicInfo topicInfo = topicInfoMap.computeIfAbsent(topic, k -> new TopicInfo(createBuiltInPartitioner(logContext, k, batchSize)));\\n286: \\n287:         // We keep track of the number of appending thread to make sure we do not miss batches in\\n288:         // abortIncompleteBatches().\\n289:         appendsInProgress.incrementAndGet();\\n290:         ByteBuffer buffer = null;\\n291:         if (headers == null) headers = Record.EMPTY_HEADERS;\\n292:         try {\\n293:             // Loop to // This call may block if we exhausted buffer space.\\n333:                     buffer = free.allocate(size, maxTimeToBlock);\\n334:                     // Update the current time in case the buffer                           byte[] value,\\n381:                                               Header[] headers,\\n382:                                               AppendCallbacks callbacks,\\n383:                                               ByteBuffer buffer,\\n384:                                               long nowMs) {\\n385:         assert partition != We also close the batch for record appends to free up\\n421:      *  resources like compression buffers. The batch will be fully closed (ie. the record batch headers will be written\\n422:      *  and memory records built) in one of the following cases (whichever comes first): right before send,\\n423:      *  if it is expired, or when the producer is closed.\\n424:      */\\n425:     private RecordAppendResult tryAppend(long timestamp, byte[] key, byte[] value, Header[] headers,\\n426:                                          Callback callback, Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, long nowMs) {\\n427:         if (closed)\\n428:             throw new KafkaException(\\\"Producer closed while send in progress\\\");\\n429:         ProducerBatch last = deque.peekLast();\\n430:         if (last != null) {\\n431:             int initialBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes();\\n432:        } else {\\n436:                 int appendedBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes() - initialBytes;\\n437:                 return new RecordAppendResult(future, deque.size() > 1 || last.isFull(), false, appendedBytes);\\n438:             }\\n439:         }\\n440:         return null;\\n441:     }\\n442: \\n443:     private boolean isMuted(TopicPartition tp) {\\n444:         return muted.contains(tp);\\n445:     }\\n446: \\n447:     public void resetNextBatchExpiryTime() {\\n448:         nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\\n449:     }\\n450: \\n451:     public void deliveryTimeoutMs);\\n456:         } else {\\n457:             log.warn(\\\"Skipping next batch expiry time update due to addition overflow: \\\"\\n458:                 + \\\"batch.createMs={}, deliveryTimeoutMs={}\\\", batch.createdMs, deliveryTimeoutMs);\\n459:         }\\n460:     }\\n461: \\n462:     /**\\n463:      * Get a list of batches which have been sitting in the accumulator too In Sender.completeBatch method, we check\\n494:      * whether the batch has reached deliveryTimeoutMs or not. Hence we do not do the delivery timeout check here.\\n495:      */\\n496:     public void reenqueue(ProducerBatch batch, long now) {\\n497:         batch.reenqueued(now);\\n498:         Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getOrCreateDeque(batch.topicPartition);\\n499:         synchronized (deque) {\\n500:             if (transactionManager != null)\\n501:                 insertInSequenceOrder(deque, batch);\\n502:             else\\n503:                 deque.addFirst(batch);\\n504:         }\\n505:     }\\n506: \\n507:     /**\\n508:      * Split the big batch that has been rejected and reenqueue the split batches in to the accumulator.\\n509:      * @return the number of split batches.\\n510:      */\\n511:     public int splitAndReenqueue(ProducerBatch bigBatch) {\\n512:         // Reset the estimated compression ratio to the initial value or the big batch compression ratio, whichever\\n513:         // is bigger. There are several different ways to do the reset. We chose the most conservative one to ensure\\n514:         // the split doesn't happen too often.\\n515:         CompressionRatioEstimator.setEstimation(bigBatch.topicPartition.topic(), compression.type(),\\n516:                                                 Math.max(1.0f, (float) bigBatch.compressionRatio()));\\n517:         Deque<ProducerBatch> dq = bigBatch.split(this.batchSize);\\n518:         int numSplitBatches = dq.size();\\n519:         Deque<ProducerBatch> partitionDequeue = getOrCreateDeque(bigBatch.topicPartition);\\n520:         while (!dq.isEmpty()) {\\n521:             ProducerBatch batch = dq.pollLast();\\n522:             incomplete.add(batch);\\n523:             // We treat the newly split batches as if they are not even tried.\\n524:             synchronized (partitionDequeue) {\\n525:                 if (transactionManager != null) {\\n526:                     // We should track the newly created batches since they already have assigned sequences.\\n527:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\\n528:                     insertInSequenceOrder(partitionDequeue, batch);\\n529:                 } else {\\n530:                     partitionDequeue.addFirst(batch);\\n531:                 }\\n532:             }\\n533:         }\\n534:         return numSplitBatches;\\n535:     }\\n536: \\n537:     // We will have to do extra work to ensure the queue is in order when requests are being retried and there are\\n538:     // multiple requests in flight to that partition. If the first in flight request fails to append, then all the\\n539:     // subsequent in flight requests will also fail because the sequence numbers will not be accepted.\\n540:     //\\n541:     // Further, once batches are being retried, we are reduced to a single in flight request for that partition. So when\\n542:     // the subsequent batches come back in sequence order, they will have to be placed further back in the queue.\\n543:     //\\n544:     // Note that this assumes that all the batches in the queue which have an assigned sequence also have the current\\n545:     // producer id. We will not attempt to reorder messages if the producer id has changed, we will throw an\\n546:     // IllegalStateException instead.\\n547:     private void insertInSequenceOrder(Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, ProducerBatch batch) {\\n548:         // When we are re-enqueueing and have enabled idempotence, the re-enqueued batch must always have a sequence.\\n549:         if (batch.baseSequence() == RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE)\\n550:             throw new IllegalStateException(\\\"Trying to re-enqueue a batch which doesn't have a sequence even \\\" +\\n551:                 \\\"though idempotency is enabled.\\\");\\n552: \\n553:         if (!transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(batch.topicPartition))\\n554:             throw new IllegalStateException(\\\"We are re-enqueueing a batch which is not tracked as part of the in flight \\\" +\\n555:                 \\\"requests. batch.topicPartition: \\\" + batch.topicPartition + \\\"; It was placed in the queue at \\\" +\\n572:                 \\\"position {}\\\", batch.baseSequence(), batch.topicPartition, orderedBatches.size());\\n573:             // Either we have reached a point where there are batches without a sequence (ie. never been drained\\n574:             // and are hence in order by default), or the batch at the front of the queue has a sequence greater\\n575:             // than the incoming batch. This is the right place to add the incoming batch.\\n576:             deque.addFirst(batch);\\n577: \\n578:             // Now we have to re insert the previously queued batches in the right order.\\n579:             for (int i = orderedBatches.size() - 1; i >= 0; --i) {\\n580:                 deque.addFirst(orderedBatches.get(i));\\n581:             }\\n582: \\n583:             // At this point, the incoming batch has been queued in the correct place according to its sequence.\\n584:         } else {\\n585:             deque.addFirst(batch);\\n586:         }\\n587:     }\\n588: \\n589:     /**\\n590:      * Add the leader to the ready nodes if the batch is ready\\n591:      *\\n592:      * @param exhausted 'true' is the buffer pool is exhausted\\n593:      * @param part The partition\\n594:      * @param leader The leader for the partition\\n595:      * @param waitedTimeMs How long batch waited\\n596:      * @param backingOff Is backing off\\n597:      * @param backoffAttempts Number of attempts for calculating backoff delay\\n598:      * @param full Is batch full\\n599:      * @param nextReadyCheckDelayMs The delay for next check\\n600:      * @param readyNodes The set of ready nodes (to be filled in)\\n601:      * @return The delay for next check\\n602:      */\\n603:     private long batchReady(boolean exhausted, TopicPartition part, Node leader,\\n604:                             long waitedTimeMs, boolean backingOff, int backoffAttempts,\\n605:                             boolean full, long nextReadyCheckDelayMs, Set<Node> readyNodes) {\\n606:         if (!readyNodes.contains(leader) && !isMuted(part)) {\\n607:             long timeToWaitMs = backingOff ? retryBackoff.backoff(backoffAttempts > 0 ? backoffAttempts - 1 : 0) : lingerMs;\\n608:             boolean expired = waitedTimeMs >= timeToWaitMs;\\n609:             boolean transactionCompleting = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isCompleting();\\n610:             boolean sendable = full\\n611:                     || expired\\n612:                     || exhausted\\n613:                     || closed\\n614:                     || flushInProgress()\\n615:                     || transactionCompleting;\\n616:             if (sendable && !backingOff) {\\n617:                 readyNodes.add(leader);\\n618:             } else {\\n619:                 long timeLeftMs = Math.max(timeToWaitMs - waitedTimeMs, 0);\\n620:                 // Note that this results in a conservative estimate since an un-sendable partition may have\\n621:                 // a leader that will later be found to have sendable data. However, this is good enough\\n622:                 // since we'll just wake up and then sleep again for the remaining time.\\n623:                 nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Math.min(timeLeftMs, nextReadyCheckDelayMs);\\n624:             }\\n625:         }\\n626:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\\n627:     }\\n628: \\n629:     /**\\n630:      * Iterate over partitions to see which one have batches ready and collect leaders of those\\n631:      * partitions into the set of ready nodes. The reason is that we build queue sizes from the batches map,\\n654:             // and if an entry is missing in the batches map, then adaptive partitioning logic\\n655:             // won't know about it and won't switch to it.\\n656:             queueSizes = new int[batches.size()];\\n657:             partitionIds = new int[queueSizes.length];\\n658:         }\\n659: \\n660:         int queueSizesIndex = -1;\\n661:         boolean exhausted = this.free.queued() > 0;\\n662:         for (Map.Entry<Integer, Deque<ProducerBatch>> entry : batches.entrySet()) {\\n663:             TopicPartition part = new TopicPartition(topic, entry.getKey());\\n664:             // Advance queueSizesIndex so that we properly index available\\n665:             // partitions.  Do it here so that it's done for all code paths.\\n666: \\n667:             Node leader = metadataSnapshot.cluster().leaderFor(part);\\n668:             if (leader != null && queueSizes != null) {\\n669:                 ++queueSizesIndex;\\n670:                 assert queueSizesIndex < queueSizes.length;\\n671:                 partitionIds[queueSizesIndex] = part.partition();\\n672:             }\\n673: \\n674:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = entry.getValue();\\n675: \\n676:             final long waitedTimeMs;\\n677:             final boolean backingOff;\\n678:             final int backoffAttempts;\\n679:             final int dequeSize;\\n680:             final boolean full;\\n681: \\n682:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(part);\\n683: \\n684:             // This loop is especially hot with large partition counts. So -\\n685: \\n686:             // 1. We should avoid code that increases synchronization between application thread calling\\n687:             // send(), and background thread running runOnce(), see https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-16226\\n688: \\n689:             // 2. We are careful to only perform the minimum required inside the\\n690:             // synchronized block, as this lock is also used to synchronize producer threads\\n691:             // attempting to append() to a partition/batch.\\n692: \\n693:             synchronized (deque) {\\n694:                 // Deques are often empty in this path, esp with large partition counts,\\n695:                 // so we exit early if we can.\\n696:                 ProducerBatch batch = deque.peekFirst();\\n697:                 if (batch == null) {\\n698:                     continue;\\n699:                 }\\n700: \\n701:                 waitedTimeMs = batch.waitedTimeMs(nowMs);\\n702:                 batch.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\\n703:                 backingOff = messages are available to send.\\n711:                 // Note that entries are currently not removed from batches when deque is empty.\\n712:                 unknownLeaderTopics.add(part.topic());\\n713:             } else {\\n714:                 if (queueSizes != null)\\n715:                     queueSizes[queueSizesIndex] = dequeSize;\\n716:                 if (partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs > 0) {\\n717:                     // Check if we want to exclude the partition from the list of available partitions\\n718:                     // if the broker hasn't responded for some time.\\n719:                     NodeLatencyStats nodeLatencyStats = nodeStats.get(leader.id());\\n720:                     if (nodeLatencyStats != null) {\\n721:                         // NOTE: there is no synchronization between reading metrics,\\n722:                         // so we read ready time first to avoid accidentally marking partition\\n723:                         // unavailable if we read while the metrics are being updated.\\n724:                         long readyTimeMs = nodeLatencyStats.readyTimeMs;\\n725:                         if (readyTimeMs - nodeLatencyStats.drainTimeMs > partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs)\\n726:                             --queueSizesIndex;\\n727:                     }\\n728:                 }\\n729: \\n730:         }\\n734: \\n735:         // We've collected the queue sizes for partitions of this topic, now we can calculate\\n736:         // load stats.  NOTE: the stats are calculated in place, modifying the\\n737:         // queueSizes array.\\n738:         topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.updatePartitionLoadStats(queueSizes, partitionIds, which any non-sendable\\n744:      * partition will be ready; Also return the flag for whether there are any unknown leaders for the accumulated\\n745:      * partition batches.\\n746:      * <p>\\n747:      * A destination node is ready to send data if:\\n748:      * <ol>\\n749:      * <li>There is at least one partition that is not backing off its send\\n750:      * <li><b>and</b> those ready(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, long nowMs) {\\n764:         Set<Node> readyNodes = new HashSet<>();\\n765:         long nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\\n766:         Set<String> {}, leader has changed, hence skipping backoff.\\\", batch);\\n806:         }\\n807:         return shouldBackoff;\\n808:     }\\n809: \\n810:     private boolean shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(ProducerBatch first, TopicPartition tp) {\\n811:         ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch;\\n812:         if (transactionManager != null) {\\n813: (!producerIdAndEpoch.isValid())\\n818:                 // we cannot send the batch until we have refreshed the producer id\\n819:                 return true;\\n820: \\n821:             if (!first.hasSequence()) {\\n822:                 if (transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(tp) && transactionManager.hasStaleProducerIdAndEpoch(tp)) {\\n823:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the partition has in-flight batches with a different epoch\\n824:                     // and/or producer ID. Otherwise, a batch with a new epoch and sequence number\\n825:                     // 0 could be written before earlier batches complete, which would cause out of sequence errors\\n826:                     return true;\\n827:                 }\\n828: \\n829:                 if (transactionManager.hasUnresolvedSequence(first.topicPartition))\\n830:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the state of previous sequence numbers\\n831:                     // is unknown. The previous batches would be unknown if they were aborted\\n832:                     // on the client after being sent to the broker at least once.\\n833:                     return true;\\n834:             }\\n835: \\n836:             int firstInFlightSequence = transactionManager.firstInFlightSequence(first.topicPartition);\\n837:             // If the queued batch already has an assigned sequence, then it is being retried.\\n838:             // In this case, we wait until the next immediate batch is ready and drain that.\\n839:             // We only move on when the next in line batch is complete (either successfully or due to\\n840:             // a fatal broker error). This effectively reduces our in flight request count to 1.\\n841:             return firstInFlightSequence != RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE && first.hasSequence()\\n842:                     && first.baseSequence() != firstInFlightSequence;\\n843:         }\\n844:         return false;\\n845:     }\\n846: \\n847:     private List<ProducerBatch> drainBatchesForOneNode(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, Node node, int maxSize, long now) {\\n848:         int size = 0;\\n849:         List<PartitionInfo> parts = metadataSnapshot.cluster().partitionsForNode(node.id());\\n850:         List<ProducerBatch> ready = new ArrayList<>();\\n851:         if (parts.isEmpty())\\n852:             return ready;\\n853:         /* to make starvation less likely each node has it's own drainIndex */\\n854:         int drainIndex = getDrainIndex(node.idString());\\n855:         int start = drainIndex = drainIndex % parts.size();\\n856:         do {\\n857:             PartitionInfo part = continue;\\n865:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getDeque(tp);\\n866:             if (deque == null)\\n867:                 continue;\\n868: \\n869:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(tp);\\n870: \\n871:             final ProducerBatch batch;\\n872:             synchronized (deque) {\\n873:                 // invariant: !isMuted(tp,now) && deque != null\\n874:                 ProducerBatch first = deque.peekFirst();\\n875:                 if (first == null)\\n876:                     continue;\\n877: \\n878:                 // first != null\\n879:                 // Only drain the batch if it is not during backoff period.\\n880:                 first.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\\n881:                 if (shouldBackoff(first.hasLeaderChangedForTheOngoingRetry(), first, first.waitedTimeMs(now)))\\n882:                     continue;\\n883: \\n884:                 if (size + first.estimatedSizeInBytes() > maxSize && !ready.isEmpty()) {\\n885:                     // there is a rare case that a single batch size is larger than the request size due to\\n886:                     // compression; in this case we will still eventually send this batch in a single request\\n887:                     break;\\n888:                 } else {\\n889:                     if (shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(first, tp))\\n890:                         break;\\n891:                 }\\n892: \\n893:                 batch = deque.pollFirst();\\n894: \\n895:                 boolean isTransactional = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isTransactional();\\n896:                 ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch =\\n897:                     transactionManager != null ? transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch() : null;\\n898:                 if (producerIdAndEpoch != null && !batch.hasSequence()) {\\n899:                     // If the producer id/epoch of the partition do not match the latest one\\n900:                     // of the producer, we update it and reset the sequence. This should be\\n901:                     // only done when all its in-flight batches have completed. This is guarantee\\n902:                     // in `shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition`.\\n903:                     transactionManager.maybeUpdateProducerIdAndEpoch(batch.topicPartition);\\n904: \\n905:                     // If the batch already has an assigned sequence, then we should not change the producer id and\\n906:                     // sequence number, since this may introduce duplicates. In particular, the previous attempt\\n907:                     // may actually have been accepted, and if we change the producer id and sequence here, this\\n908:                     // attempt will also be accepted, causing a duplicate.\\n909:                     //\\n910:                     // Additionally, we update the next sequence number bound for the partition, and also have\\n911:                     // the transaction manager track the batch so as to ensure that sequence ordering is maintained\\n912:                     // even if we receive out of order responses.\\n913:                     batch.setProducerState(producerIdAndEpoch, transactionManager.sequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition), isTransactional);\\n914:                     transactionManager.incrementSequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition, batch.recordCount);\\n915:                     log.debug(\\\"Assigned producerId {} and producerEpoch {} to batch with base sequence \\\" +\\n916:                             \\\"{} being sent to partition {}\\\", producerIdAndEpoch.producerId,\\n917:                         producerIdAndEpoch.epoch, batch.baseSequence(), outside the lock\\n924:             // close() is particularly expensive\\n925:             batch.close();\\n926:             size += batch.records().sizeInBytes();\\n927:      }\n252:         }\n253: \n254:         return false;\n255:     }\n256: \n257:     /**\n258:      * Add a record to the accumulator, return the append result\n259:      * <p>\n260:      * The   int partition,\n277:                                      long timestamp,\n278:                                      byte[] key,\n279:                                      byte[] value,\n280:                                      Header[] headers,\n281:                                      AppendCallbacks callbacks,\n282:                                      long maxTimeToBlock,\n283: -> new TopicInfo(createBuiltInPartitioner(logContext, k, batchSize)));\n286: \n287:         // We keep track of the number of appending thread to make sure we do not miss batches in\n288:         //                        continue;\n318: \n319:                     RecordAppendResult appendResult = tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callbacks, dq, nowMs);\n320:                     if AbstractRecords.estimateSizeInBytesUpperBound(\n330:                             RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression.type(), key, value, headers));\n331:                     log.trace(\"Allocating a new {} byte message buffer for topic {} partition {} with remaining timeout {}ms\", size, topic, effectivePartition, maxTimeToBlock);\n332:                     // This call may block if we exhausted buffer space.\n333:                     buffer = free.allocate(size, maxTimeToBlock);\n334:                     // Update the current time in case the buffer allocation topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.updatePartitionInfo(partitionInfo, appendResult.appendedBytes, cluster, enableSwitch);\n352:                     return appendResult;\n353:                 }\n354:             }\n355:         } finally {\n356:             free.deallocate(buffer);\n357:             appendsInProgress.decrementAndGet();\n358:         }\n359:     }\n360: \n361:     /**\n362:      * Append a We also close the batch for record appends to free up\n421:      *  resources like compression buffers. The batch will be fully closed (ie. the record batch headers will be written\n422:      *  and memory records built) in one of the following cases (whichever comes first): right before send,\n423:      *  if it is expired, or when the producer is closed.\n424:      */\n425:     private RecordAppendResult tryAppend(long timestamp, byte[] key, byte[] value, Header[] headers,\n426:                                          Callback callback, Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, long nowMs) {\n427:         if (closed)\n428:             throw new KafkaException(\"Producer closed while send in progress\");\n429:         ProducerBatch last = deque.peekLast();\n430:         if (last != null) {\n431:             int initialBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes();\n432:             FutureRecordMetadata future = last.tryAppend(timestamp, key, value, headers, callback, nowMs);\n433:             if (future == null) {\n434:                 last.closeForRecordAppends();\n435:             } else {\n436:                 int appendedBytes = last.estimatedSizeInBytes() - initialBytes;\n437:                 return new RecordAppendResult(future, deque.size() > 1 || last.isFull(), false, appendedBytes);\n438:             }\n439:         }\n440:         return null;\n441:     }\n442: \n443:     private boolean isMuted(TopicPartition tp) {\n444:         return muted.contains(tp);\n445:     }\n446: \n447:     public void resetNextBatchExpiryTime() {\n448:         nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\n449:     }\n450: \n451:     public void maybeUpdateNextBatchExpiryTime(ProducerBatch batch) {\n452:         if (batch.createdMs + deliveryTimeoutMs  > 0) {\n453:             // the non-negative check is to guard us against potential overflow due to setting\n454:             // a large value for deliveryTimeoutMs\n455:             nextBatchExpiryTimeMs = Math.min(nextBatchExpiryTimeMs, batch.createdMs + deliveryTimeoutMs);\n456:         } else {\n457:             log.warn(\"Skipping next batch expiry time update due to addition overflow: \"\n458:                 + \"batch.createMs={}, deliveryTimeoutMs={}\", batch.createdMs, deliveryTimeoutMs);\n459:         }\n460:     }\n461: \n462:     /**\n463:      * Get a list of batches which have been sitting in the accumulator too long and need to be expired.\n464:      */\n465:     public List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches(long now) {\n466:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = new ArrayList<>();\n467:         for (TopicInfo topicInfo : topicInfoMap.values()) {\n468:             for (Deque<ProducerBatch> deque : topicInfo.batches.values()) {\n469:                 // expire the batches in the order of sending\n470:                 synchronized (deque) {\n471:                     while (!deque.isEmpty()) {\n472:                         ProducerBatch batch = deque.getFirst();\n473:                         if (batch.hasReachedDeliveryTimeout(deliveryTimeoutMs, now)) {\n474:                             deque.poll();\n475:                             batch.abortRecordAppends();\n476:                             expiredBatches.add(batch);\n477:                         } else {\n478:                             maybeUpdateNextBatchExpiryTime(batch);\n479:                             break;\n480:                         }\n481:                     }\n482:                 }\n483:             }\n484:         }\n485:         return expiredBatches;\n486:     }\n487: \n488:     public long getDeliveryTimeoutMs() {\n489:         return deliveryTimeoutMs;\n490:     }\n491: \n492:     /**\n493:      * Re-enqueue the given record batch in the accumulator. In Sender.completeBatch method, we check\n494:      * whether the batch has reached deliveryTimeoutMs or not. Hence we do not do the delivery timeout check here.\n495:      */\n496:     public void reenqueue(ProducerBatch batch, long now) {\n497:         batch.reenqueued(now);\n498:         Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getOrCreateDeque(batch.topicPartition);\n499:         synchronized (deque) {\n500:             if (transactionManager != null)\n501:                 insertInSequenceOrder(deque, batch);\n502:             else\n503:                 deque.addFirst(batch);\n504:         }\n505:     }\n506: \n507:     /**\n508:      * Split the big batch that has been rejected and reenqueue the split batches in to the accumulator.\n509:      * @return the number of split batches.\n510:      */\n511:     public int splitAndReenqueue(ProducerBatch bigBatch) {\n512:         // Reset the estimated compression ratio to the initial value or the big batch compression ratio, whichever\n513:         // is bigger. There are several different ways to do the reset. We chose the most conservative one to ensure\n514:         // the split doesn't happen too often.\n515:         CompressionRatioEstimator.setEstimation(bigBatch.topicPartition.topic(), compression.type(),\n516:                                                 Math.max(1.0f, (float) bigBatch.compressionRatio()));\n517:         Deque<ProducerBatch> dq = bigBatch.split(this.batchSize);\n518:         int numSplitBatches = dq.size();\n519:         Deque<ProducerBatch> partitionDequeue = getOrCreateDeque(bigBatch.topicPartition);\n520:         while (!dq.isEmpty()) {\n521:             ProducerBatch batch = dq.pollLast();\n522:             incomplete.add(batch);\n523:             // We treat the newly split batches as if they are not even tried.\n524:             synchronized (partitionDequeue) {\n525:                 if (transactionManager != null) {\n526:                     // We should track the newly created batches since they already have assigned sequences.\n527:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\n528:                     insertInSequenceOrder(partitionDequeue, batch);\n529:                 } else {\n530:                     partitionDequeue.addFirst(batch);\n531:                 }\n532:             }\n533:         }\n534:         return numSplitBatches;\n535:     }\n536: \n537:     // We will have to do extra work to ensure the queue is in order when requests are being retried and there are\n538:     // multiple requests in flight to that partition. If the first in flight request fails to append, then all the\n539:     // subsequent in flight requests will also fail because the sequence numbers will not be accepted.\n540:     //\n541:     // Further, once batches are being retried, we are reduced to a single in flight request for that partition. So when\n542:     // the subsequent batches come back in sequence order, they will have to be placed further back in the queue.\n543:     //\n544:     // Note that this assumes that all the batches in the queue which have an assigned sequence also have the current\n545:     // producer id. We will not attempt to reorder messages if the producer id has changed, we will throw an\n546:     // IllegalStateException instead.\n547:     private void insertInSequenceOrder(Deque<ProducerBatch> deque, ProducerBatch batch) {\n548:         // When we are re-enqueueing and have enabled idempotence, the re-enqueued batch must always have a sequence.\n549:         if (batch.baseSequence() == RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE)\n550:             throw new IllegalStateException(\"Trying to re-enqueue a batch which doesn't have a sequence even \" +\n551:                 \"though idempotency is enabled.\");\n552: \n553:         if (!transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(batch.topicPartition))\n554:             throw new IllegalStateException(\"We are re-enqueueing a batch which is not tracked as part of the in flight \" +\n555:                 \"requests. batch.topicPartition: \" + batch.topicPartition + \"; batch.baseSequence: \" + batch.baseSequence());\n556: \n557:         ProducerBatch firstBatchInQueue = deque.peekFirst();\n558:         if (firstBatchInQueue != null && firstBatchInQueue.hasSequence() && firstBatchInQueue.baseSequence() < batch.baseSequence()) {\n559:             // The incoming batch can't be inserted at the front of the queue without violating the sequence ordering.\n560:             // This means that the incoming batch should be placed somewhere further back.\n561:             // We need to find the right place for the incoming batch and insert it there.\n562:             // We will only enter this branch if we have multiple inflights sent to different brokers and we need to retry\n563:             // the inflight batches.\n564:             //\n565:             // Since we reenqueue exactly one batch a time and ensure that the queue is ordered by sequence always, it\n566:             // is a simple linear scan of a subset of the in flight batches to find the right place in the queue each time.\n567:             List<ProducerBatch> orderedBatches = new ArrayList<>();\n568:             while (deque.peekFirst() != null && deque.peekFirst().hasSequence() && deque.peekFirst().baseSequence() < batch.baseSequence())\n569:                 orderedBatches.add(deque.pollFirst());\n570: \n571:             log.debug(\"Reordered incoming batch with sequence {} for partition {}. It was placed in the queue at \" +\n572:                 \"position {}\", batch.baseSequence(), batch.topicPartition, orderedBatches.size());\n573:             // Either we have reached a point where there are batches without a sequence (ie. never been drained\n574:             // and are hence in order by default), or the batch at the front of the queue has a sequence greater\n575:             // than the incoming batch. This is the right place to add the incoming batch.\n576:             deque.addFirst(batch);\n577: \n578:             // Now we have to re insert the previously queued batches in the right order.\n579:             for (int i = orderedBatches.size() - 1; i >= 0; --i) {\n580:                 deque.addFirst(orderedBatches.get(i));\n581:             }\n582: \n583:             // At this point, the incoming batch has been queued in the correct place according to its sequence.\n584:         } else {\n585:             deque.addFirst(batch);\n586:         }\n587:     }\n588: \n589:     /**\n590:      * Add the leader to the ready nodes if the batch is ready\n591:      *\n592:      * @param exhausted 'true' is the buffer pool is exhausted\n593:      * @param part The partition\n594:      * @param leader The leader for the partition\n595:      * @param waitedTimeMs How long batch waited\n596:      * @param backingOff Is backing off\n597:      * @param backoffAttempts Number of attempts for calculating backoff delay\n598:      * @param full Is batch full\n599:      * @param nextReadyCheckDelayMs The delay for next check\n600:      * @param readyNodes The set of ready nodes (to be filled in)\n601:      * @return The delay for next check\n602:      */\n603:     private long batchReady(boolean exhausted, TopicPartition part, Node leader,\n604:                             long waitedTimeMs, boolean backingOff, int backoffAttempts,\n605:                             boolean full, long nextReadyCheckDelayMs, Set<Node> readyNodes) {\n606:         if (!readyNodes.contains(leader) && !isMuted(part)) {\n607:             long timeToWaitMs = backingOff ? retryBackoff.backoff(backoffAttempts > 0 ? backoffAttempts - 1 : 0) : lingerMs;\n608:             boolean expired = waitedTimeMs >= timeToWaitMs;\n609:             boolean transactionCompleting = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isCompleting();\n610:             boolean sendable = full\n611:                     || expired\n612:                     || exhausted\n613:                     || closed\n614:                     || flushInProgress()\n615:                     || transactionCompleting;\n616:             if (sendable && !backingOff) {\n617:                 readyNodes.add(leader);\n618:             } else {\n619:                 long timeLeftMs = Math.max(timeToWaitMs - waitedTimeMs, 0);\n620:                 // Note that this results in a conservative estimate since an un-sendable partition may have\n621:                 // a leader that will later be found to have sendable data. However, this is good enough\n622:                 // since we'll just wake up and then sleep again for the remaining time.\n623:                 nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Math.min(timeLeftMs, nextReadyCheckDelayMs);\n624:             }\n625:         }\n626:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\n627:     }\n628: \n629:     /**\n630:      * Iterate over partitions to see which one have batches ready and collect leaders of those\n631:      * partitions into the set of ready nodes.  If partition has no leader, add the topic to the set\n632:      * of topics with no leader.  This function also calculates stats for adaptive partitioning.\n633:      *\n634:      * @param metadataSnapshot      The cluster metadata\n635:      * @param nowMs                 The current time\n636:      * @param topic                 The topic\n637:      * @param topicInfo             The topic info\n638:      * @param nextReadyCheckDelayMs The delay for next check\n639:      * @param readyNodes            The set of ready nodes (to be filled in)\n640:      * @param unknownLeaderTopics   The set of topics with no leader (to be filled in)\n641:      * @return The delay for next check\n642:      */\n643:     private long partitionReady(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, long nowMs, String topic,\n644:                                 TopicInfo topicInfo,\n645:                                 long nextReadyCheckDelayMs, Set<Node> readyNodes, Set<String> unknownLeaderTopics) {\n646:         ConcurrentMap<Integer, Deque<ProducerBatch>> batches = topicInfo.batches;\n647:         // Collect the queue sizes for available partitions to be used in adaptive partitioning.\n648:         int[] queueSizes = null;\n649:         int[] partitionIds = null;\n650:         if (enableAdaptivePartitioning && batches.size() >= metadataSnapshot.cluster().partitionsForTopic(topic).size()) {\n651:             // We don't do adaptive partitioning until we scheduled at least a batch for all\n652:             // partitions (i.e. we have the corresponding entries in the batches map), we just\n653:             // do uniform.  The reason is that we build queue sizes from the batches map,\n654:             // and if an entry is missing in the batches map, then adaptive partitioning logic\n655:             // won't know about it and won't switch to it.\n656:             queueSizes = new int[batches.size()];\n657:             partitionIds = new int[queueSizes.length];\n658:         }\n659: \n660:         int queueSizesIndex = -1;\n661:         boolean exhausted = this.free.queued() > 0;\n662:         for (Map.Entry<Integer, Deque<ProducerBatch>> entry : batches.entrySet()) {\n663:             TopicPartition part = new TopicPartition(topic, entry.getKey());\n664:             // Advance queueSizesIndex so that we properly index available\n665:             // partitions.  Do it here so that it's done for all code paths.\n666: \n667:             Node leader = metadataSnapshot.cluster().leaderFor(part);\n668:             if (leader != null && queueSizes != null) {\n669:                 ++queueSizesIndex;\n670:                 assert queueSizesIndex < queueSizes.length;\n671:                 partitionIds[queueSizesIndex] = part.partition();\n672:             }\n673: \n674:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = entry.getValue();\n675: \n676:             final long waitedTimeMs;\n677:             final boolean backingOff;\n678:             final int backoffAttempts;\n679:             final int dequeSize;\n680:             final boolean full;\n681: \n682:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(part);\n683: \n684:             // This loop is especially hot with large partition counts. So -\n685: \n686:             // 1. We should avoid code that increases synchronization between application thread calling\n687:             // send(), and background thread running runOnce(), see https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-16226\n688: \n689:             // 2. We are careful to only perform the minimum required inside the\n690:             // synchronized block, as this lock is also used to synchronize producer threads\n691:             // attempting to append() to a partition/batch.\n692: \n693:             synchronized (deque) {\n694:                 // Deques are often empty in this path, esp with large partition counts,\n695:                 // so we exit early if we can.\n696:                 ProducerBatch batch = deque.peekFirst();\n697:                 if (batch == null) {\n698:                     continue;\n699:                 }\n700: \n701:                 waitedTimeMs = batch.waitedTimeMs(nowMs);\n702:                 batch.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\n703:                 backingOff = shouldBackoff(batch.hasLeaderChangedForTheOngoingRetry(), batch, waitedTimeMs);\n704:                 backoffAttempts = batch.attempts();\n705:                 dequeSize = deque.size();\n706:                 full = dequeSize > 1 || batch.isFull();\n707:             }\n708: \n709:             if (leader == null) {\n710:                 // This is a partition for which leader is not known, but messages are available to send.\n711:                 // Note that entries are currently not removed from batches when deque is empty.\n712:                 unknownLeaderTopics.add(part.topic());\n713:             } else {\n714:                 if (queueSizes != null)\n715:                     queueSizes[queueSizesIndex] = dequeSize;\n716:                 if (partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs > 0) {\n717:                     // Check if we want to exclude the partition from the list of available partitions\n718:                     // if the broker hasn't responded for some time.\n719:                     NodeLatencyStats nodeLatencyStats = nodeStats.get(leader.id());\n720:                     if (nodeLatencyStats != null) {\n721:                         // NOTE: there is no synchronization between reading metrics,\n722:                         // so we read ready time first to avoid accidentally marking partition\n723:                         // unavailable if we read while the metrics are being updated.\n724:                         long readyTimeMs = nodeLatencyStats.readyTimeMs;\n725:                         if (readyTimeMs - nodeLatencyStats.drainTimeMs > partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs)\n726:                             --queueSizesIndex;\n727:                     }\n728:                 }\n729: \n730:                 nextReadyCheckDelayMs = batchReady(exhausted, part, leader, waitedTimeMs, backingOff,\n731:                     backoffAttempts, full, nextReadyCheckDelayMs, readyNodes);\n732:             }\n733:         }\n734: \n735:         // We've collected the queue sizes for partitions of this topic, now we can calculate\n736:         // load stats.  NOTE: the stats are calculated in place, modifying the\n737:         // queueSizes array.\n738:         topicInfo.builtInPartitioner.updatePartitionLoadStats(queueSizes, partitionIds, queueSizesIndex + 1);\n739:         return nextReadyCheckDelayMs;\n740:     }\n741: \n742:     /**\n743:      * Get a list of nodes whose partitions are ready to be sent, and the earliest time at which any non-sendable\n744:      * partition will be ready; Also return the flag for whether there are any unknown leaders for the accumulated\n745:      * partition batches.\n746:      * <p>\n747:      * A destination node is ready to send data if:\n748:      * <ol>\n749:      * <li>There is at least one partition that is not backing off its send\n750:      * <li><b>and</b> those partitions are not muted (to prevent reordering if\n751:      *   {@value org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.ProducerConfig#MAX_IN_FLIGHT_REQUESTS_PER_CONNECTION}\n752:      *   is set to one)</li>\n753:      * <li><b>and <i>any</i></b> of the following are true</li>\n754:      * <ul>\n755:      *     <li>The record set is full</li>\n756:      *     <li>The record set has sat in the accumulator for at least lingerMs milliseconds</li>\n757:      *     <li>The accumulator is out of memory and threads are blocking waiting for data (in this case all partitions\n758:      *     are immediately considered ready).</li>\n759:      *     <li>The accumulator has been closed</li>\n760:      * </ul>\n761:      * </ol>\n762:      */\n763:     public ReadyCheckResult ready(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, long nowMs) {\n764:         Set<Node> readyNodes = new HashSet<>();\n765:         long nextReadyCheckDelayMs = Long.MAX_VALUE;\n766:         Set<String> unknownLeaderTopics = new HashSet<>();\n767:         // Go topic by topic so that we can get queue sizes for partitions in a topic and calculate\n768:         // cumulative frequency table (used in partitioner).\n769:         for (Map.Entry<String, TopicInfo> topicInfoEntry : this.topicInfoMap.entrySet()) {\n770:             final String topic = topicInfoEntry.getKey();\n771:             nextReadyCheckDelayMs = partitionReady(metadataSnapshot, nowMs, topic, topicInfoEntry.getValue(), nextReadyCheckDelayMs, readyNodes, unknownLeaderTopics);\n772:         }\n773:         return new ReadyCheckResult(readyNodes, nextReadyCheckDelayMs, unknownLeaderTopics);\n774:     }\n775: \n776:     /**\n777:      * Check whether there are any batches which haven't been drained\n778:      */\n779:     public boolean hasUndrained() {\n780:         for (TopicInfo topicInfo : topicInfoMap.values()) {\n781:             for (Deque<ProducerBatch> deque : topicInfo.batches.values()) {\n782:                 synchronized (deque) {\n783:                     if (!deque.isEmpty())\n784:                         return true;\n785:                 }\n786:             }\n787:         }\n788:         return false;\n789:     }\n790: \n791:     private boolean shouldBackoff(boolean hasLeaderChanged, final ProducerBatch batch, final long waitedTimeMs) {\n792:         boolean shouldWaitMore = batch.attempts() > 0 && waitedTimeMs < retryBackoff.backoff(batch.attempts() - 1);\n793:         boolean shouldBackoff = !hasLeaderChanged && shouldWaitMore;\n794:         if (log.isTraceEnabled()) {\n795:             if (shouldBackoff) {\n796:                 log.trace(\n797:                     \"For {}, will backoff\", batch);\n798:             } else {\n799:                 log.trace(\n800:                     \"For {}, will not backoff, shouldWaitMore {}, hasLeaderChanged {}\", batch,\n801:                     shouldWaitMore, hasLeaderChanged);\n802:             }\n803:         } else if (log.isDebugEnabled() && hasLeaderChanged) {\n804:             // Add less-verbose log at DEBUG.\n805:             log.debug(\"For {}, leader has changed, hence skipping backoff.\", batch);\n806:         }\n807:         return shouldBackoff;\n808:     }\n809: \n810:     private boolean shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(ProducerBatch first, TopicPartition tp) {\n811:         ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch;\n812:         if (transactionManager != null) {\n813:             if (!transactionManager.isSendToPartitionAllowed(tp))\n814:                 return true;\n815: \n816:             producerIdAndEpoch = transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch();\n817:             if (!producerIdAndEpoch.isValid())\n818:                 // we cannot send the batch until we have refreshed the producer id\n819:                 return true;\n820: \n821:             if (!first.hasSequence()) {\n822:                 if (transactionManager.hasInflightBatches(tp) && transactionManager.hasStaleProducerIdAndEpoch(tp)) {\n823:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the partition has in-flight batches with a different epoch\n824:                     // and/or producer ID. Otherwise, a batch with a new epoch and sequence number\n825:                     // 0 could be written before earlier batches complete, which would cause out of sequence errors\n826:                     return true;\n827:                 }\n828: \n829:                 if (transactionManager.hasUnresolvedSequence(first.topicPartition))\n830:                     // Don't drain any new batches while the state of previous sequence numbers\n831:                     // is unknown. The previous batches would be unknown if they were aborted\n832:                     // on the client after being sent to the broker at least once.\n833:                     return true;\n834:             }\n835: \n836:             int firstInFlightSequence = transactionManager.firstInFlightSequence(first.topicPartition);\n837:             // If the queued batch already has an assigned sequence, then it is being retried.\n838:             // In this case, we wait until the next immediate batch is ready and drain that.\n839:             // We only move on when the next in line batch is complete (either successfully or due to\n840:             // a fatal broker error). This effectively reduces our in flight request count to 1.\n841:             return firstInFlightSequence != RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE && first.hasSequence()\n842:                     && first.baseSequence() != firstInFlightSequence;\n843:         }\n844:         return false;\n845:     }\n846: \n847:     private List<ProducerBatch> drainBatchesForOneNode(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, Node node, int maxSize, long now) {\n848:         int size = 0;\n849:         List<PartitionInfo> parts = metadataSnapshot.cluster().partitionsForNode(node.id());\n850:         List<ProducerBatch> ready = new ArrayList<>();\n851:         if (parts.isEmpty())\n852:             return ready;\n853:         /* to make starvation less likely each node has it's own drainIndex */\n854:         int drainIndex = getDrainIndex(node.idString());\n855:         int start = drainIndex = drainIndex % parts.size();\n856:         do {\n857:             PartitionInfo part = parts.get(drainIndex);\n858: \n859:             TopicPartition tp = new TopicPartition(part.topic(), part.partition());\n860:             updateDrainIndex(node.idString(), drainIndex);\n861:             drainIndex = (drainIndex + 1) % parts.size();\n862:             // Only proceed if the partition has no in-flight batches.\n863:             if (isMuted(tp))\n864:                 continue;\n865:             Deque<ProducerBatch> deque = getDeque(tp);\n866:             if (deque == null)\n867:                 continue;\n868: \n869:             OptionalInt leaderEpoch = metadataSnapshot.leaderEpochFor(tp);\n870: \n871:             final ProducerBatch batch;\n872:             synchronized (deque) {\n873:                 // invariant: !isMuted(tp,now) && deque != null\n874:                 ProducerBatch first = deque.peekFirst();\n875:                 if (first == null)\n876:                     continue;\n877: \n878:                 // first != null\n879:                 // Only drain the batch if it is not during backoff period.\n880:                 first.maybeUpdateLeaderEpoch(leaderEpoch);\n881:                 if (shouldBackoff(first.hasLeaderChangedForTheOngoingRetry(), first, first.waitedTimeMs(now)))\n882:                     continue;\n883: \n884:                 if (size + first.estimatedSizeInBytes() > maxSize && !ready.isEmpty()) {\n885:                     // there is a rare case that a single batch size is larger than the request size due to\n886:                     // compression; in this case we will still eventually send this batch in a single request\n887:                     break;\n888:                 } else {\n889:                     if (shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition(first, tp))\n890:                         break;\n891:                 }\n892: \n893:                 batch = deque.pollFirst();\n894: \n895:                 boolean isTransactional = transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isTransactional();\n896:                 ProducerIdAndEpoch producerIdAndEpoch =\n897:                     transactionManager != null ? transactionManager.producerIdAndEpoch() : null;\n898:                 if (producerIdAndEpoch != null && !batch.hasSequence()) {\n899:                     // If the producer id/epoch of the partition do not match the latest one\n900:                     // of the producer, we update it and reset the sequence. This should be\n901:                     // only done when all its in-flight batches have completed. This is guarantee\n902:                     // in `shouldStopDrainBatchesForPartition`.\n903:                     transactionManager.maybeUpdateProducerIdAndEpoch(batch.topicPartition);\n904: \n905:                     // If the batch already has an assigned sequence, then we should not change the producer id and\n906:                     // sequence number, since this may introduce duplicates. In particular, the previous attempt\n907:                     // may actually have been accepted, and if we change the producer id and sequence here, this\n908:                     // attempt will also be accepted, causing a duplicate.\n909:                     //\n910:                     // Additionally, we update the next sequence number bound for the partition, and also have\n911:                     // the transaction manager track the batch so as to ensure that sequence ordering is maintained\n912:                     // even if we receive out of order responses.\n913:                     batch.setProducerState(producerIdAndEpoch, transactionManager.sequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition), isTransactional);\n914:                     transactionManager.incrementSequenceNumber(batch.topicPartition, batch.recordCount);\n915:                     log.debug(\"Assigned producerId {} and producerEpoch {} to batch with base sequence \" +\n916:                             \"{} being sent to partition {}\", producerIdAndEpoch.producerId,\n917:                         producerIdAndEpoch.epoch, batch.baseSequence(), tp);\n918: \n919:                     transactionManager.addInFlightBatch(batch);\n920:                 }\n921:             }\n922: \n923:             // the rest of the work by processing outside the lock\n924:             // close() is particularly expensive\n925:             batch.close();\n926:             size += batch.records().sizeInBytes();\n927:             ready.add(batch);\n928: \n929:             batch.drained(now);\n930:         } while (start != drainIndex);\n931:         return ready;\n932:     }\n933: \n934:     private int getDrainIndex(String idString) {\n935:         return nodesDrainIndex.computeIfAbsent(idString, s -> 0);\n936:     }\n937: \n938:     private void updateDrainIndex(String idString, int drainIndex) {\n939:         nodesDrainIndex.put(idString, drainIndex);\n940:     }\n941: \n942:     /**\n943:      * Drain all the data for the given nodes and collate them into a list of batches that will fit\n944:      * within the specified size on a per-node basis. This method attempts to avoid choosing the same\n945:      * topic-node over and over.\n946:      *\n947:      * @param metadataSnapshot  The current cluster metadata\n948:      * @param nodes             The list of node to drain\n949:      * @param maxSize           The maximum number of bytes to drain\n950:      * @param now               The current unix time in milliseconds\n951:      * @return A list of {@link ProducerBatch} for each node specified with total size less than the\n952:      * requested maxSize.\n953:      */\n954:     public Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> drain(MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot, Set<Node> nodes, int maxSize, long now) {\n955:         if (nodes.isEmpty())\n956:             return Collections.emptyMap();\n957: \n958:         Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = new HashMap<>();\n959:         for (Node node : nodes) {\n960:             List<ProducerBatch> ready = drainBatchesForOneNode(metadataSnapshot, node, maxSize, now);\n961:             batches.put(node.id(), ready);\n962:         }\n963:         return batches;\n964:     }\n965: \n966:     public void updateNodeLatencyStats(Integer nodeId, long nowMs, boolean canDrain) {\n967:         // Don't bother with updating stats if the feature is turned off.\n968:         if (partitionAvailabilityTimeoutMs <= 0)\n969:             return;\n970: \n971:         // When the sender gets a node (returned by the ready() function) that has data to send\n972:         // but the node is not ready (and so we cannot drain the data), we only update the\n973:         // ready time, then the difference would reflect for how long a node wasn't ready\n974:         // to send the data. until the send is complete\n1067:      */\n1068:     public void awaitFlushCompletion() throws InterruptedException {\n1069:         try {\n1070:             // Obtain a copy of all of the incomplete ProduceRequestResult(s) at the time of the flush.\n1071:             // We must be careful not to hold a reference to the ProduceBatch(s) so that garbage\n1072:             // collection can occur on the contents.\n1073:             // The sender will remove ProducerBatch(s) from the original incomplete collection.\n1074:             //\n1075:             // We use awaitAllDependents() here instead of await() to ensure that if any batch\n1076:             // was split into multiple batches, we wait for all the split batches to complete.\n1077:             // This is required to guarantee that all records sent before flush()\n1078:             // must be fully complete, including records in split batches.\n1079:             for (ProduceRequestResult result : this.incomplete.requestResults())\n1080:                 result.awaitAllDependents();\n1081:         } finally {\n1082:             this.flushesInProgress.decrementAndGet();\n1083:         }\n1084:     }\n1085: \n1086:     /**\n1087:      * Check whether there are any pending batches (whether sent or unsent).\n1088:      */\n1089:     public boolean hasIncomplete() {\n1090:         return !this.incomplete.isEmpty();\n1091:     }\n1092: \n1093:     /**\n1094:      * This function is only called when sender is closed forcefully. It will fail all the\n1095:      * incomplete batches and return.\n1096:      */\n1097:     public void abortIncompleteBatches() {\n1098:         // We need to keep aborting the incomplete batch until no thread is trying to append to\n1099:         // 1. Avoid losing batches.\n1100:         // 2. Free up memory in case appending threads are blocked on buffer full.\n1101:         // This is a tight loop but should be able to get through very quickly.\n1102:         do {\n1103:             abortBatches();\n1104:         } while (appendsInProgress());\n1105:         // After this point, no thread will append any messages because they will see the close\n1106:         // flag set. We need to do the last abort after no thread was appending in case there was a new\n1107:         // batch appended by the last appending thread.\n1108:         abortBatches();\n1109:         this.topicInfoMap.clear();\n1110:     }\n1111: \n1112:     /**\n1113:      * Go through incomplete batches and abort them.\n1114:      */\n1115:     private void abortBatches() {\n1116: **Batch Management** \u2014 Maintains per-partition queues of `ProducerBatch` objects\n2. **Batch Accumulation** \u2014 Accumulates records into batches for efficient transmission\n3. **Ready Checks** \u2014 Determines which batches are ready to send (ready nodes)\n4. **Batch Draining** \u2014 Returns ready batches for transmission to the broker\n5. **Adaptive Partitioning** \u2014 Implements adaptive partitioning logic through `PartitionerConfig`\n\nThe core data structure is:\n```java\nprivate final ConcurrentMap<TopicPartition, Deque<ProducerBatch>> batches;\n```\n\nThis structure operates at **batch granularity**, not record granularity, which justifies the rename to `BatchAccumulator`.\n\n## Refactoring Statistics\n\n| Category | Count |\n|----------|-------|\n| Files renamed **Batch Management** \u2014 Maintains per-partition queues of `ProducerBatch` objects\n2. **Batch Accumulation** \u2014 Accumulates records into batches for efficient transmission\n3. **Ready Checks** \u2014 Determines which batches are ready to send (ready nodes)\n4. **Batch Draining** \u2014 Returns ready batches for transmission to the broker\n5. **Adaptive Partitioning** \u2014 Implements adaptive partitioning logic through `PartitionerConfig`\n\nThe core data structure is:\n```java\nprivate final ConcurrentMap<TopicPartition, Deque<ProducerBatch>> batches;\n```\n\nThis structure # Kafka Producer Refactoring: RecordAccumulator → BatchAccumulator

## Executive Summary

This refactoring renames the `RecordAccumulator` class to `BatchAccumulator` throughout the Apache Kafka producer subsystem. The new name better reflects the class's true responsibility: managing per-partition queues of `ProducerBatch` objects at batch granularity, not individual records.

## Files Examined

### Production Code
- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BatchAccumulator.java** — Core class definition; renamed from RecordAccumulator.java; manages producer batches
- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java** — Uses BatchAccumulator as a field; creates instances; uses BatchAccumulator.PartitionerConfig, BatchAccumulator.AppendCallbacks, BatchAccumulator.RecordAppendResult
- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java** — Uses BatchAccumulator as a field; calls methods on accumulator; uses BatchAccumulator.ReadyCheckResult
- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BuiltInPartitioner.java** — Comment references to BatchAccumulator partitioning logic
- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java** — Comment references to BatchAccumulator batch abort logic
- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/Node.java** — Comment references to BatchAccumulator.ready() performance-critical code

### Test Code
- **clients/src/test/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BatchAccumulatorTest.java** — Test class; renamed from RecordAccumulatorTest.java; tests BatchAccumulator functionality
- **clients/src/test/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducerTest.java** — Tests KafkaProducer; uses Ba
... (truncated)
